Jamison Brereton

18 (844)
Death, etc.
Saс╣Гkusuka Y─Бm─Бyana
14 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except 11 prast─Бrapaс╣Еkti, 13 jagat─л, 14 anuс╣гс╣нubh
This lovely hymn falls into several sections, each treating the end of the funeral service. The first six verses depict the mourners leaving the service and returning to their lives. Death is dismissed in verse 1, and in verses 2тАУ3 the living turn back to an enhanced life, full of тАЬdancing and laughterтАЭ (vs. 3). They are separated from death by a barrier (vs. 4); in the later ritual a stone is set down near the grave. Verses 5тАУ6 are especially concerned with the orderly sequence of life and death, in particular the fear that the younger will die before their elders and disrupt the proper sequence (see esp. 5cd).
The next three verses (7тАУ9) have been much discussed, especially in the context of тАЬsutteeтАЭ (sat─л) or widow-burning, though the verses are emphatically not a depic tion thereof. From verse 8 it appears that the widow lies down, temporarily, beside her dead husband, but is summoned back to life and indeed symbolically reborn to become the wife of a new husband (quite possibly her brother-in-law, in levirate marriage). The happy women in verse 7 apparently approach the funeral pyre to adorn the widow for her return to life. A similar тАЬreturn to lifeтАЭ is granted the dead manтАЩs bow in verse 9, where someone, quite possibly the dead manтАЩs son, repossesses the bow to put it to future use.

The burial is the subject of verses 10тАУ13, with an emphasis on the softness and gentleness of the welcoming earth, both mother and bride, which lies lightly on the dead man. Verse 13 forms a sort of ring with verse 1, with both expressing a prohibition against harm with the same construction and the same root тИЪriс╣г (1d m─Б╠Б…r─лriс╣гaс╕е, 13b m─Б╠Б…riс╣гam). This ring defines the final verse (14) as outside the hymn proper, and other indications support this extra-hymnic status. It is in dimeter meter, instead of the trimeter that prevails elsewhere, and the A┼Ыval─Бyana Gr╠еhya S┼лtra, which treats the ritual usage of all the other verses, ignores it, as does the medieval commentator S─Бyaс╣Зa. The sense of this verse is also much disputed. Many scholars think that the poet is predicting his own future death, on a day that is approaching him, in the first hemistich, and in the second he restrains his speech in anticipation. (As Geldner says, rather more dramatically than usual, тАЬder Rest ist SchweigenтАЭ [the rest is silence].) In contrast, we consider this to belong to the typi cal genre of hymn-final meta-poetic verses, in which the poet comments on his own skill in producing the poem that precedes. By this interpretation, the first half-verse concerns the well-conducted funeral that has just taken place, while the second refers specifically to the poetтАЩs taming and controlling the speech that accompanied that ritual.

010-019 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton

The next ten hymns (X.10тАУ19) form a Yama cycle, though the subject matter found in the individual hymns is quite various. Yama, the son of Vivasvant, is king of the land of the dead because he was the first mortal to die. Yet he was apparently born immortal (see esp. I.83.5) and chose to become mortal, subject to death, тАЬfor the sake of the gods…and for the sake of offspringтАЭ (X.13.4). The opening hymn in the cycle, the dialogue of Yama and his twin sister Yam─л, on the fraught topic of embarking on incestuous sex in order to produce offspring, addresses YamaтАЩs change of status and his choice, but in a deliberately oblique and misleading fashion, as Yama spurns the sexual advances of his sister, and at the end of their bitter argument there seems little likelihood of children. The last six hymns in this cycle (X.14тАУ19) are collectively known as funeral hymns. The first, X.14, is devoted especially to Yama in his role as king of the realm of the dead, while the others, especially 15тАУ18, concern various aspects of death and the treatment of the deadтАФfor example, the forefathers who preceded us to YamaтАЩs realm in X.15, the cremation fire in X.16, the funeral itself in X.

The intermediate hymns, X.11тАУ13, have less superficially clear connections to the Yama saga, but both X.12 (vss. 6тАУ7) and X.13 (vss. 4тАУ5) make important comments on Yama and on YamaтАЩs choice.

There is also an underlying unifying theme, that of duality and twinned-ness: the absolute disjunction between and the ultimate complementarity and unity of the mortal and the immortal, life and death, men and gods, men and women, heaven and earth, sacred and profane. It is appropriate that the cycle should begin with the dialogue between the primal twins, Yama and Yam─л, whose very names mean тАЬtwinтАЭ and who bridge the gap between mortal and immortal.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDepart, Mс╣Ыtyu, by a different path; by that which is your own, and distinct from the path of the gods; Ispeak to you who have eyes, who have ears; do no harm to our offspring, nor to our male progeny.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Offspring:praj─Бm = feminine le offspring; or, santatim, descendants, family successors

Jamison Brereton

Depart, Death, along the further path, which is your own, different from the one leading to the gods.
To you who possess eyes and who listen do I speak: do not harm our offspring nor our heroes.

Griffith

Go hence, O Death, pursue thy special pathway apart from that which Gods are wont to travel.
To thee I say it who hast eyes and hearest: Touch not our offspring, injure not our heroes.

Macdonell

Depart, O Death, along the farthest pathway, Which is thine own, not that by mortals trodden. I speak to thee that hast both eyes and hearing: Do not our offspring injure nor our heroes.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf, avoiding the path of death, you go (on the path of he gods), assuming a longer and better life, (myfriends), then may you, (O sacrificers), diligent in sacrifice, enriched with progeny and affluence, be cleansed andpure.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Be cleansed and pure: ┼Ыuddhaс╕е = pure from the decay caused by the sins accusative ulated in a former life;

P┼лtaс╕е = pure from the decay caused by the sins of the present life

Jamison Brereton

Effacing the footprint of death when you have gone, establishing for yourselves a longer, more extended lifetime,
swelling up with offspring and wealth, become cleansed and purified, o you who are worthy of the sacrifice.

Griffith

As ye have come effacing Mrtyu’s footstep, to further times prolonging your existence,
May ye be rich in children and possessions. cleansed, purified, and meet for sacrificing.

Macdonell

Since ye have come, the trace of death effacing, Till future days prolonging your existence: With offspring and with riches thriving greatly, Do ye, O pious men, be pure and holy.

Geldner

Nachdem ihr gegangen seid, des Todes Spur verwischend und euer Leben noch weiter verl├дngernd, so werdet, an Kindern und Reichtum zunehmend, rein und lauter, ihr Opferw├╝rdigen!

Grassmann

Des Todes Spur verwischend, als ihr kamet, und lange euer k├╝nft’ges Leben dehnend, An Reichthum wachsend und an Schar der Kinder, o fromme, werdet reinen Sinns und lauter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay those who are living remain separate from the dead; may our invocation of the gods today besuccessful; let us go forward to dancing and laughter, assuming a longer and better life.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Go forward: or, with ourfaces to the east

Jamison Brereton

These the living have turned aside from the dead. The invocation of the gods has become favorable for us today.
We have gone facing forward to dancing, to laughter, establishing for ourselves a longer, more extended lifetime.

Griffith

Divided from the dead are these, the living: now be our calling on the Gods successful.
We have gone forth for dancing and for laughter, tofurther times prolonging our existence.

Macdonell

These living men have from the dead been parted; Our calling of the gods is now auspicious. We have come near, prepared for dance and laughter, Till future days prolonging our existence.

Geldner

Diese Lebenden haben sich jetzt von den Toten geschieden; die G├╢tteranrufung ist uns heute gegl├╝ckt. Wir sind dem Tanz und Lachen entgegen gegangen, unser Leben noch weiter verl├дngernd.

Grassmann

Getrennt sind diese lebenden vom todten, der Gottesdienst ward heute uns zum Heile; Wir sind genaht bereit zu Tanz und Scherzen, auf lange unser k├╝nft’ges Leben dehnend.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдкрд╛рд╖рд╛рдгрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЬреАрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдЬреАрд╡рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рднреНрдпрд╕реНрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореЗрд╡рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐рдВ рдореГрддреНрдпреЛрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд╛рдирднреВрддрдВ рдкрд╛рд╖рд╛рдгрдВ рджрдзрд╛рдорд┐ рдирд┐рджрдзрд╛рдорд┐ ред рддрддрдГ рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЬреАрд╡рддрд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЕрдкрд░рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ рдПрддрдореН рдЗрдордореН рдЕрд░реНрдердореН ред рдЕрд░реНрддреЗрд░рд┐рджрдВ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдорд░рдгрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдВ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдорд╛ рдЧрд╛рддреН рдорд╛ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдПрддрджрд░реНрдердВ рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐рдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпрд╛рдореАрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдкреБрд░реВрдЪреАрдГ рдмрд╣реНрд╡рдЮреНрдЪрдирд╛ рдмрд╣реБрдЧрдордирд╛рдГ рд╢рддрдВ рд╢рд░рджрдГ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдиреН рдЬреАрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреНрддреБ ред рддрдерд╛ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреЗрди рд╢рд┐рд▓реЛрдЪреНрдЪрдпреЗрди рдореГрддреНрдпреБрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдорд╛рд░рдХрдореЗрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХрдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ рджрдзрддрд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдирд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI erect this circle (of stones) for (the protection of) the living, that none other of them may approach thislimit; may they live a hundred years, occupied by many holy works, and keep death hidden by this mound.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I erectthis circle of stones: after the burning of the body, the Adhvaryu is to raise a bank or lump or earth betwen thevillage where the deceased lived and the cemetery, as a rampart against death (Mah─лdhara, Yajus. 35.15);

Paridhi = a stone rampart (p─Бс╣г─Бс╣Зam)

Jamison Brereton

I set down this barrier here for the living. Let no one of these later go to this goal.
Let them live for a hundred ample autumns. Let them conceal death with a mountain.

Griffith

Here I erect this rampart for the living; let none of these, none other, reach this limit.
May they survive a hundred lengthened autumns, and may they bury Death beneath this mountain.

Macdonell

For those that live do I set up this limit, May now no other one this goal encounter. May they exist a hundred ample autumns: By this stone may they death remove far from them.

Geldner

Diese Schranke setze ich f├╝r die Lebenden , nicht m├╢ge ein anderer unter ihnen zu diesem Ziele gelangen. Sie sollen hundert reichliche Herbste leben und den Tod mit diesem Berge absperren.

Grassmann

Die Schutzwehr setz’ ich hier f├╝r die, die leben, dass ihrer keiner lauf nach diesem Ziele, Sie m├╢gen hundert reiche Herbste leben, durch diesen Stein den Tod von sich hinwegthun.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs days pass along in succession; as season are duly followed by seasons; as the successor doesnot abandon his predecessor, so, Dh─Бt─Б, support the lives of these (my kinsmen).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As the successor: i.e., as ason does not leave his father by dying first

Jamison Brereton

Just as the days follow each upon the last, just as the seasons follow straightaway upon the seasons,
so, o Ordainer, arrange their lifetimes, so that the later does not leave behind the earlier.

Griffith

As the days follow days in close succession, as with the seasons duly come the seasons,
As each successor fails not his foregoer, so form the lives of these, O great Ordainer.

Macdonell

As days in order follow one another, As seasons duly alternate with seasons. And as the later ne’er forsakes the earlier, So settle thou the lives of these, Ordainer.

Geldner

Wie die Tage in richtiger Folge erscheinen, wie die Jahreszeiten um Jahreszeiten richtig kommen, also, o Sch├╢pfer, regle ihre Lebenszeiten, da├Я nicht der J├╝ngere den ├Дlteren verlasse!

Grassmann

Wie Tag auf Tag in steter Reihe folget, wie Zeit auf Zeit in gradem Weg dahingeht, Die folgende sich eng der fr├╝hern anschliesst, so bild’, o Sch├╢pfer, ihre Lebenstage.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдореГрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджрдпрдГ рдЬрд░рд╕рдВ рдЬрд░рд╛рдВ рд╡реГрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛ рдпреВрдпрдореН рдЖрдпреБрдГ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореН рдЖ рд░реЛрд╣рдд рдЕрдзрд┐рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардд ред рдЕрдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЖрдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпреЗрдг ред рдЕрд╡реНрдпрдпреАрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЛ рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдардГ ред рдЬреНрдпреЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдпрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рдпрддрд┐ рд╕реНрде рдпрддреНрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛ рднрд╡рде ред рдпрдЪреНрдЫрдмреНрджрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕реЛ рдбрддрд┐рдГ ред рд╕реБрдЬрдирд┐рдорд╛ рд╢реЛрднрдирдЬрдирдирдГ рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╕рдЬреЛрд╖рд╛рдГ рднрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрдЧрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдЗрд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рдГ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдЬреАрд╡рд╕реЗ рдЬреАрд╡рдирд╛рдп рджреАрд░реНрдШрдВ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдореН рдЖрдпреБрдГ рдХрд░рддрд┐ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(You kinsmen of the dead man), choosing old age, attain length of life, striving one after the other, howmany soever you may be; may Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, the creator.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Striving one after the other: the eldest first; of good racesof men, being at one (with you), grant you (busy) at this (sacrifice), a long life

Jamison Brereton

Mount your lifetime, choosing old age, taking your place each following the last, as many as you are.
Here will Tvaс╣гс╣нar, affording good birth, in concert (with the Wives of the Gods), make a long lifetime for you to live.

Griffith

Live your full lives ap! find old age delightful, all of you striving one behind the other.
May Tvastar, maker of fair things, be gracious and lengthen out the days of your existence.

Macdonell

Do ye attain long life, old age selecting, As many as you are combined in order. May Tvaс╣гс╣нar, well-disposed, the skilled creator, Produce forthwith long life for your existence.

Geldner

Steiget auf, langes Leben, das Alter euch ausbittend, in der richtigen Reihenfolge euch anschlie├Яend, so viele wie ihr seid! M├╢ge Tvastri, der gute Geburten gibt, damit einverstanden euch hienieden lange Frist zum Leben gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Des Lebens Kraft erreicht zu hohem Alter, wie viel ihr seid, zu einem Zug verbunden; Der Gutes zeugt, mit euch vereinigt, Tvaschtar verschaffe lange Dauer eurem Leben.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet these women who are not widows, who have good husbands, enter (anointed) with unguent andbutter. Let women without tears, without sorrow, and decorated with jewels, first proceed to the house.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These women here, non-widows with good husbandsтАФlet them, with fresh butter as ointment, approach together.
Without tears, without afflictions, well-jeweled, let the wives first mount the womb.

Griffith

Let these unwidowed dames with noble husbands adorn themselves with fragrant balm and unguent.
Decked with fair jewels, tearless, free from sorrow, first let the dames go up to where he lieth.

Macdonell

These women here, non-widows, with good husbands, Let them provide themselves with fat and butter. Tearless and free from care, well-decked with jewels, Let first these wives ascend the place of mourning.

Geldner

Diese Frauen, Nichtwitwen mit guten Gatten, sollen mit Butter als Augensalbe gesalbt sich niederlegen. Ohne Tr├дnen, frei von Krankheit, mit sch├╢nen Kleinodien sollen die Frauen zuerst das Lager wieder besteigen.

Grassmann

Mit fettem Oel und Salben m├╢gen kommen die Weiber hier, verm├дhlt und nicht verwitwet, Die St├дtte m├╢gen sie zuerst beschreiten, die sch├╢ngeschm├╝ckten, ohne Leid und Thr├дnen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRise, woman, (and go) to the world of living beings; come, this man near whom you sleep is lifeless;you have enjoyed this state of being the wife of your husband, the suitor who took you by the band.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This verseis to be spoken by the husband’s brother, etc., to the wife of the dead man, and he is to make her leave herhusband’s body: (─А┼Ыval─Бyana Gс╣Ыhya S┼лtra, 4.2); go to beings = go to the home of the living, i.e., your sons,grandsons etc.

Jamison Brereton

тАЬArise, woman, to the world of the living. You lie beside him whose life is gone. Come here!
You have come into existence now as wife of a husband who has
grasped your hand and wishes to have you.тАЭ

Griffith

Rise, come unto the world of life, O woman: come, he is lifeless by whose side thou liest.
Wifehood with this thy husband was thy portion, who took thy hand and wooed thee as a lover.

Macdonell

Arise, come to the world of life, O woman; Thou liest here by one whose breath has left him. Come: thou hast entered upon the wifehood Of this thy lord who takes thy hand and woos thee.

Geldner

Erhebe dich, o Weib, zur Welt der Lebenden; du liegst bei diesem Entseelten, komm! Du bist eingetreten in diesen Ehestand mit einem Gatten, der deine Hand ergreift und dich besitzen will.

Grassmann

Erhebe dich, o Weib, zur Welt des Lebens; du liegst vor dem, dess Hauch entflohn ist, komm nun; Der deine Hand einst fasste und dich freite, des Gatten Ehe hast du nun vollendet.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTaking his bow from the hand of the dead man, for the sake of our vigour, energy and strength, (I say)you are there; may we (who are) here, blessed with male offspring, overcome all the enemies who assail us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Taking the bow from the hand of the dead for our dominion, luster, and strength,
you there and we hereтАФmay we with good heroes win all contests and hostile engagements.

Griffith

From his dead hand I take the bow be carried, that it may be our power and might and glory.
There art thou, there; and here with noble heroes may we o’ercome all hosts that fight against us.

Macdonell

From the dead hand I take the bow he wielded, To win for us dominion, might, and glory. Thou there, we here, rich in heroic offspring, Will vanquish all assaults of every foeman.

Grassmann

Den Bogen nehm’ ich aus der Hand des Todten, f├╝r uns zur Herrschaft, uns zu Glanz und St├дrke; Du dort und wir hienieden tapfre Helden, wir wollen schlagen jedes Feindes Angriff.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡рд┐ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫреНрд╡рдЮреНрдЪрд╕реНрд╡ ред рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдВрдЧрддреЛрдЪреНрдЫреНрд╡рд╛рд╕рдореЗрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реБ ред рдЕрдзрд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреНрдорд╛ рдХреГрдерд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдорд╛ рдирд┐ рдмрд╛рдзрдерд╛рдГ рдорд╛ рд╕рдВрдкреАрдбрдп ред рддрдерд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╕реВрдкрд╛рдпрдирд╛ рд╢реЛрднрдиреЛрдкрдЧрдордирд╛ рд╕реВрдкрдЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдХрд╛ рднрд╡реЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕реВрдкрд╡рдЮреНрдЪрдирд╛ред рдЙрдкрд╡рдЮреНрдЪрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд▓рдореНрднрдирдореН ред рд╢реЛрднрдирдкреНрд░рд▓рдореНрднрд╛ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реНрдард╛ рднрд╡ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдореН рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпрдВ рдмрд╛рд▓рдХрдВ рд╕рд┐рдЪрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рдпрдерд╛ рдЖрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдпрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рджреНрдзреЗ рднреВрдорд┐ рдПрдирдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдерд┐рд░реВрдкрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрднрд┐ рдКрд░реНрдгреБрд╣рд┐ рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEarth, rise up above him; oppress him not; be attentive to him (and) comfortable; cover him up, earth,as a mother covers her child with the skirt of her garment.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Earth, rise up above him: i.e., so as to give himbreathing room; while reciting this verse, dust is to be scattered over the grave;

Comfortable: s┼лpava├▒can─Б =deceiving well; treat him kindly for the sake of the sacrifice; fondle him, lull him to rest; supratiс╣гс╣нh─Б bhava = be

Jamison Brereton

Arch up, Earth; do not press down. Become easy to approach for him, easy to curl up in.
Like a mother her son with her hem, cover him, Earth.

Griffith

Heave thyself, Earth, nor press thee downward heavily: afford him easy access, gently tending him.
Cover him, as a mother wraps her skirt about her child, O Earth.

Macdonell

Wide open, earth, O press not heavily on him; Be easy of approach to him, a refuge safe; As with a robe a mother hides Her son, so shroud this man, O earth.

Geldner

W├╢lbe dich auf, o Erde, bedr├╝cke ihn nicht, gib ihm guten Zugang und guten Unterschlupf! Wie die Mutter ihren Sohn mit einem Zipfel, so decke ihn zu, o Erde!

Grassmann

Er├╢ffne dich, o Erde; nicht bedr├дnge ihn, gew├дhr ihm leichten Eingang, sichern Zufluchtsort, Umh├╝ll ihn, Erde, wie den Sohn die Mutter h├╝llt in ihr Gewand.

Elizarenkova

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

May the earth stand piled high above him; verily upheld by a 1000 props. May it be the house dripping with ghee; Through eternity may he be sheltered here!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBring them back again, render them obedient; may Indra restor ethem; may Agni bring them near.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

MayIndra restore them: make them obedient to you

Jamison Brereton

Let the earth stay arching up. For let a thousand (house)posts be fixed in (her).
Let the house be dripping with ghee. Let it always be sheltering to
him there.

Griffith

Now let the heaving earth be free from motion: yea,- let a thousand clods remain above him.
Be they to him a home distilling fatness, here let them ever be his place of refuge.

Macdonell

Now opening wide may here the earth stand steadfast, May here a thousand columns rise to prop her; May here those mansions ever drip with butter, And here be always shelter to protect him.

Geldner

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay they come back to me and be fostered under this (their) protector; do you Agni, keep them here;may whatever wealth (there is) remain here.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I prop up the earth from you. Setting down this earth clod here, let me not be harmed.
Let the forefathers uphold this pillar for you. There let Yama fix your seats.

Griffith

I stay the earth from thee, while over thee I place this piece of earth. May I be free from injury.
Here let the Fathers keep this pillar firm for thee, and there let Yama make thee an abiding-place.

Macdonell

For thee I now prop up the earth around thee here; In lowering this clod may I receive no harm. May the Fathers hold up for thee this column, And Yama here provide for thee fit mansions.

Geldner

Ich stemme die Erde ├╝ber dir empor. Wenn ich diese Scholle niederlege, m├╢chte ich keinen Schaden nehmen. Diese S├дule sollen die V├дter dir festhalten. Yama soll dir dort eine Wohnst├дtte errichten!

Grassmann

Rings um dich her befest’ge ich die Erde nun, nicht schad’ es mir, wenn ich die Scholle senk’ herab; Die V├дter m├╢gen diese S├дule halten dir, dort aber Jama dir bereiten einen Sitz.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдирдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЬрдкрддрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдереНрдпрддреЗ рд╣реЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреВрдЬреНрдпреЗ рдЕрд╣рдирд┐ рддрджреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреЗ рд╕рдВрд╡рддреНрд╕- рд╕рдЩреНрдХреБрд╕реБрдХрдореГрд╖рд┐рдВ рдЖрджрдзреБрдГ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ ред рдХрд┐рдорд┐рд╡ рдЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдмрд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рдкрд░реНрдгрдорд┐рд╡ рдкрдХреНрд╖рдорд┐рд╡ рдкрдХреНрд╖рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдмрд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рдореВрд▓реЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЬрдЧрддреНрдореВрд▓реЗ рддреНрд╡рдпрд┐ рдорд╛рдВ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрд┐рддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рдЕрддреЛрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдВ рдкреВрдЬреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реВрдкрд╛рдВ рдЬрдЧреГрдн рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдг ред рдХрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдВ рдЖрд╢реБрдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирдВ рд╣рдпрдВ рд░рд╢рдирдпрд╛ рд░рдЬреНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдХрд░реНрдгрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдорддреНрдХреГрддрд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдВ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдгреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее резрек реерд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди рддрдореЛрд╣рд╛рд░реНрджрдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдпрдиреН ред рдкреБрдорд░реНрдерд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реЛрджреЗрдпрд╛рджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рддреАрд░реНрдердорд╣реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее рез реердЗрддрд┐рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдзрд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡реИрджрд┐рдХрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрдХрд╢реНрд░реАрд╡реАрд░рдмреБрдХреНрдХрднреВрдкрд╛рд▓рд╕рд╛рдореНрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдзреБрд░рдиреНрдзрд░рдг рд╕рд╛- рдпрдгрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗрдг рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рдорд╛рдзрд╡реАрдпреЗ рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗ рдЛрдХреНрд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рднрд╖реНрдпреЗ рд╕рдкреНрддрдорд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke the knowledge of the plural ce, of their going, of their coming, of their departure, of theirwandering, of their returning; (I invoke) him who is their keeper.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

On the day facing me [=today] they have set (him=dead man) down like a feather from an arrow.
The speech facing me I have grasped, like a horse by its halter.

Griffith

Even as an arrow’s feathers, they have set me on a fitting day.
The fit word have I caught and held as ’twere a courser with the rein.

Geldner

An einem nachfolgenden Tage setzen sie mich bei, wie man die Feder des Pfeils feststeckt. Ich habe die Rede zur├╝ckgehalten wie ein Ro├Я mit dem Z├╝gel.

Grassmann

Am n├дchstvergangnen Tage hat man mich wie Federn an den Pfeil gef├╝gt; ich halte das Wort zur├╝ck wie ein Ross am Z├╝gel.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдкрд┐рддреГрдореЗрдзрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдкрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛
  • рд╕рдЩреНрдХреБрд╕реБрдХреЛ рдпрд╛рдорд╛рдпрдирдГ
  • рдирд┐рдЪреГрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдЧрд╛рдиреНрдзрд╛рд░рдГ
рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдиреЗ-рдЕрд╣рдирд┐) рд╕рд╛рдордиреЗ рдЖрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдордп рджрд┐рди рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЖрдЧрд╛рдореА рд╕рдордп рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд (рдорд╛рдореН) рдореЛрдХреНрд╖ рдЪрд╛рд╣рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдореБрдЭ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реА рдЬрди рдХреЛ (рдЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдГ-рдкрд░реНрдгрдореН-рдЗрд╡ рдЖрджрдзреБрдГ) рдмрд╛рдгрдЪрд╛рд▓рдХ рдмрд╛рдг рдХреЗ рдкрд░реНрд╡ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд▓реЛрд╣рдкрддреНрд░ рдХрд╛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЖрдзрд╛рди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрд╕реА рднрд╛рдБрддрд┐ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдореБрдЭреЗ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд░реВрдк рд╕реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдЕрдиреНрджрд░ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реЗ (рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдЬрдЧреНрд░рдн) рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреАрди-рддреЗрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЛ рддреВ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░, рдЙрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрди рд╣реБрдП рддреБрдЭрдХреЛ (рд░рд╢реНрдордпрдГ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдВ рдпрдерд╛) рдШрд╛рд╕ рдЖрджрд┐ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐ рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЛ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓ рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рдРрд╕реЗ рддреБрдЭреЗ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрдХреВрд▓ рдмрдирд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реВрдБ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХреЗ рдЕрдЧреНрд░рд┐рдо рднрд╛рдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрдд рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдХ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдХреЛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╕реМрдВрдк рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рдгреА рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмрд╛рдг рдХреЗ рдлрд▓рдХ рдХреЛ рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдкрд░ рдзрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдРрд╕реЗ рд╣реАред рд╡рд╣ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рдЕрдкрдиреА рдФрд░ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓ рдмрдирд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдРрд╕реА рд╣реА рд╣реИ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдШреЛреЬреЗ рдХреЛ рдЕрдиреБрдХреВрд▓ рдмрдирд╛рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдП рдШрд╛рд╕ рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдиреЗ-рдЕрд╣рдирд┐) рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреЗ рджрд┐рдиреЗ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрд╜рдЧреНрд░рд┐рдореЗ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдЬреАрд╡рдиреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧреЗ-рдореЛрдХреНрд╖реЗ тАЬрдЕрд╣рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГтАЭ [рд╢режрезрейредреиредрезредрем] рддрдиреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗ-рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН (рдорд╛рдореН) рдореЛрдХреНрд╖рдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдВ рдЬрдирдВ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкрд░реНрдгрдореН-рдЗрд╡-рдЖрджрдзреБрдГ) рдЗрд╖реБрдЪрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛ рдЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдмрд╛рдгрд╕реНрдп рдкрд░реНрдгрдореН рд▓реЛрд╣рдкрддреНрд░рдВ рдлрд▓рдХрдорд╛рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐-рдЖрдзрд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЦрд▓реБ рдорд╛рдорд╛рдзреЗрд╣рд┐ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдордиреН ! рдкреНрд░рдгрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордХреЗ рдзрдиреБрд╖рд┐ тАЬрдкреНрд░рдгрд╡реЛ рдзрдиреБрдГ рд╢рд░реЛ рд╣реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╛тАЭ [рдореБрдгреНрдбрежреиредреиредрек] рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рдпрдерд╛ (рдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреАрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдВ рдЬрдЧреНрд░рдн) рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреАрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдЧрдиреНрддреНрд░реАрдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рдЪрдореН тАЬрдкреНрд░рддреАрдЪреА рдЕрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреАтАЭ [рдирд┐рд░реБрежрейредрел] рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рдг рддрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рдиреНрдирдВ рд╕рдиреНрддрдВ рдЪрд╛рд╣рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН (рд░рд╢рдирдпрд╛-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдВ рдпрдерд╛) рдУрд╖рдзреНрдпрд╛ рдШрд╛рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдпрдерд╛ тАЬрдУрд╖рдзрдпреЛ рд░рд╢рдирд╛тАЭ [рдХрежрекрезредрек] рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрдХреВрд▓рдВ рдирдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрдХреВрд▓рдВ рдирдпрд╛рдорд┐ реерезрекрее
